## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species' concentration over time. In chemical kinetics, dA/dt is typically governed by rate laws that depend on concentration A raised to some power (reaction order), with possible time-dependent forcing or complex multi-step mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (intermediate species in sequential reactions)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-varying external influence)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with background source/sink)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate constants (c0 < 0) indicate consumption/decay of reactant A, while positive values indicate production
- Integer or half-integer exponents on concentration often correspond to elementary reaction steps or radical mechanisms
- Rational functions of concentration (A/(c+A) or A/(c+A²)) indicate surface catalysis or enzyme saturation where active sites become limiting
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not explicitly on t, the system is autonomous and follows a standard rate law from mass-action kinetics
- Explicit time dependence in the rate expression suggests external forcing (e.g., photolysis, temperature ramp) or that A represents an intermediate in a multi-species system where other species have been eliminated
- Sum of exponential terms in t suggests the system is part of a coupled linear ODE system (consecutive or parallel first-order reactions)
- Products of A with polynomial or rational functions of A suggest autocatalytic or cooperative reaction mechanisms
- Square root dependence on concentration (A**0.5) often indicates radical chain mechanisms where dissociation equilibria are involved

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK0)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_z*A**c3/(c4*A**c5 + c6)
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to analyze each candidate to determine if it can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.18997742423620262*A**2 + 0.45987487478174419*A**2/(0.7497988950401423*A**4 + 1)`

Let me simplify the GT. The GT is a function of A only (no t dependence). It has the form:

`f(A) = c_a * A^2 + c_b * A^2 / (c_c * A^4 + 1)`

This is a rational function. Let me combine over a common denominator:

`f(A) = [c_a * A^2 * (c_c * A^4 + 1) + c_b * A^2] / (c_c * A^4 + 1)`
`= [c_a * c_c * A^6 + c_a * A^2 + c_b * A^2] / (c_c * A^4 + 1)`
`= [c_a * c_c * A^6 + (c_a + c_b) * A^2] / (c_c * A^4 + 1)`

With numerical values:
- c_a = -0.18998
- c_b = 0.45987
- c_c = 0.74980

Numerator: `-0.14245 * A^6 + 0.26990 * A^2`
Denominator: `0.74980 * A^4 + 1`

So GT = `(-0.14245 * A^6 + 0.26990 * A^2) / (0.74980 * A^4 + 1)`

Key properties of GT:
1. It's a function of A only (no t)
2. It's a rational function of A
3. It's even in A (only even powers)
4. The structure is: `α*A^2 + β*A^2/(γ*A^4 + 1)`

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `A**3*c0/(A + c1) + A*c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(A**2*c5 + 1) + c6)`

Contains sin and log - these are transcendental functions that cannot equal a rational function unless their coefficients are zero. If c3=0, we get `A^3*c0/(A+c1) + A*c2`. This is a rational function: `[c0*A^3 + c2*A*(A+c1)]/(A+c1) = [c0*A^3 + c2*A^2 + c1*c2*A]/(A+c1)`. This has odd-degree terms and a linear denominator, not matching GT's structure (A^4 denominator). Cannot match.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `A**3*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*log(A**2*c5 + 1))`

Contains sin(log(...)) - transcendental. Setting c2=0: `A^3*c0 + A*c1` - polynomial with odd powers only. GT has even powers. Cannot match.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `A**3*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*log(A**2*c5 + 1)) + c6*exp(A*c7)`

Setting c2=0, c6=0: `A^3*c0 + A*c1` - odd powers only. No match.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `A*c0 + c1 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*log(A*c5 + 1))`

Setting c2=0: `A*c0 + c1` - linear. Cannot match GT.

Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `A**3*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5*exp(c6*sin(A*c7 + c8))`

Setting c3=0, c5=0 (or c6=0): `A^3*c0 + A*c1` - odd powers. No match.

Wait, let me reconsider. Setting c0=0, c1=0, c5=0 (or c6=0): `A^c2*c3*log(A*c4+1)`. This is a log function, not rational. No match.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(A**2*c7 + 1) + c8)`

Setting c1=0, c2=0, c5=0: `A^2*c0`. Just a monomial. Cannot match GT which has a rational component.

Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `A**3*c0/(A + c1) + A*c2/(A + c1) + A*c3/(A + c1) + c4*exp(c5*sin(A*c6 + c7))`

Setting c4=0 (or c5=0): `[A^3*c0 + A*(c2+c3)]/(A+c1)`. Linear denominator, cannot produce A^4 denominator. No match.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `A**3*c0 + A*c1/(A + c2) + A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6*log(A*c7 + 1)`

Setting c6=0: `A^3*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2) + A^c3*c4`.

Combined: `c0*A^3 + c4*A^2 + c1*A/(A+c2)`. The rational part has denominator (A+c2), not (A^4+const). Cannot match GT.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 9:** `A**3*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3 + c4*log(A**2*c5 + 1)) + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)`

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 10:** `A**2*c0 + A*c1/(A + c2) + A*c3/(A**2 + c4) + A**c5*c6*sin(A*c7 + c8)`

Numerator: `c0*A^2*(A+c2)(A^2+c4) + c1*A*(A^2+c4) + c3*A*(A+c2)`

This is degree 5 polynomial over degree 3 polynomial. GT is degree 6 over degree 4. Structure mismatch.

`A^2*c2 + A*c3/(A+c4) + A*c5/(A^2+c6)`

What if I keep c0 ≠ 0? Then I have `A^3*c0/(A+c1)` plus the rest. Common denominator would be `(A+c1)(A+c4)(A^2+c6)` which is degree 4. That's promising!

Let me compute: `A^3*c0/(A+c1) + A^2*c2 + A*c3/(A+c4) + A*c5/(A^2+c6)`

Common denominator: `(A+c1)(A+c4)(A^2+c6)`

Numerator:
- `c0*A^3*(A+c4)(A^2+c6)` = `c0*A^3*(A^3 + c4*A^2 + c6*A + c4*c6)` = `c0*(A^6 + c4*A^5 + c6*A^4 + c4*c6*A^3)`
- `c2*A^2*(A+c1)(A+c4)(A^2+c6)` = `c2*A^2*(A^2+(c1+c4)*A+c1*c4)(A^2+c6)` = very high degree (degree 6 from A^2 * degree 4)

Wait, this gives degree 8 numerator over degree 4 denominator. That's too high.

Actually, GT has degree 6 numerator over degree 4 denominator, which simplifies to a degree 2 polynomial plus a proper fraction. Let me reconsider.

GT = `α*A^2 + β*A^2/(γ*A^4+1)`. The denominator is `γ*A^4+1`.

For Candidate 46, the denominator would be `(A+c1)(A+c4)(A^2+c6)` = `A^4 + (c1+c4)*A^3 + (c1*c4+c6)*A^2 + (c1+c4)*c6*A + c1*c4*c6`.

For this to match `γ*A^4+1`, we need:
- Coefficient of A^3: `c1+c4 = 0`, so c4 = -c1
- Coefficient of A^2: `c1*c4+c6 = c1*(-c1)+c6 = -c1^2+c6 = 0`, so c6 = c1^2
- Coefficient of A: `(c1+c4)*c6 = 0` ✓ (since c1+c4=0)
- Constant: `c1*c4*c6 = c1*(-c1)*c1^2 = -c1^4`

So denominator = `A^4 - c1^4`, and we need this proportional to `γ*A^4+1`. So `-c1^4` corresponds to `1/γ`, meaning `c1^4 = -1/γ` which requires c1^4 < 0. Impossible since c1^4 ≥ 0.

So the denominator cannot match. No match.

Candidate 46 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Let me reconsider - I've rejected all candidates. Let me re-examine the GT more carefully and see if I missed any possible structural match.

GT = `-0.18998*A^2 + 0.45987*A^2/(0.74980*A^4 + 1)`

This is `A^2 * [-0.18998 + 0.45987/(0.74980*A^4 + 1)]`
`= A^2 * [-0.18998*(0.74980*A^4+1) + 0.45987] / (0.74980*A^4+1)`
`= A^2 * [-0.14245*A^4 - 0.18998 + 0.45987] / (0.74980*A^4+1)`
`= A^2 * [-0.14245*A^4 + 0.26989] / (0.74980*A^4+1)`
`= [-0.14245*A^6 + 0.26989*A^2] / (0.74980*A^4+1)`

The key feature is a degree 4 denominator with only A^4 and constant terms. None of the candidates can produce this denominator structure through their rational components.
